Title: under attack again
Post by: Dread Pirate Roberts on April 28, 2013, 09:57 am
UPDATE (05/04/2013 2120 UTC): The site is back up.  I'm not going to say we are out of the woods yet, but unless something unexpected happens, we should remain up for the foreseeable future.

UPDATE (05/05/2013 0100 UTC): We're still doing battle with this attacker.  It seems he has prepared for this for a long time and has many tactics.  We continue to use every resource at our disposal to overcome this situation.  Thank you for your patience.

UPDATE (05/03/2013 0545 UTC): The attacks have been coming non-stop since my last update.  We've been able to keep the site open more than half the time with only minor issues such as limited image uploading for vendors.  Every hour we are making progress and I am feeling much more confident that we will come out on top within the next few days.  Still, expect some unannounced down-time here and there.

UPDATE (05/01/2013 0238 UTC): Silk Road is open and accessible.  As soon as the attacker finds out, he will likely change his tactics and try to take the site down again.  Hopefully he won't be able to, but time will tell.

UPDATE (04/30/2013 2022 UTC): Still working on a solution.  I haven't given up hope that we will be able to go forward as a public market without limiting access.  We are putting all of our efforts into making that a reality.  If that changes, I will let you know here.

UPDATE (04/30/2013 0035 UTC): We have come a long way in the battle, but still do not have the upper hand.  It's looking more and more like a restructuring of the tor software or even the tor network will be required to mitigate the kind of attack we are under.  If this can be solved by modifying the tor client software running the silk road .onion, then it will be a matter of patching and redeploying the hidden service.  If it is a network issue, it will require the cooperation of the Tor developers, or running a new network of nodes.  I haven't given up hope for a faster solution, but if one can not be found, then we will move to a semi private scheme where users will be given access through many private URLs.  I'll keep everyone updated on how we will move forward, but please be prepared for a few more days at the least of no access.

UPDATE (04/29/2013 0715 UTC): Just want to let you all know I'm still here and we're still doing battle behind the scenes to get the forums and main site running again.  It is incredibly discouraging to have everything we've worked so hard for taken down by some anonymous and malevolent person, but your kind words of encouragement do wonders for our moral.  We are on the cutting edge of anonymity technology here.  The attacks being used against us MUST be overcome if Silk Road and any anonymous public sites are to have a future.  Thank you again for your patience with all of this, and pray that we make it through stronger than we started.

We are being attacked once more.  This time the forums are under attack as well.  Access is intermittent, so hopefully some of you can read this.  We are doing everything possible to overcome this latest attack.  Please be patient while we find a solution.

Title: Re: under attack again
Post by: scout on April 28, 2013, 10:54 pm
http://dkn255hz262ypmii.onion/index.php?topic=77808
http://dkn255hz262ypmii.onion/index.php?topic=151488

Those are just two of the many, many threads discussing this.  He is free to access SR how he wants, and Liberte is definitely a great set up, but why leave the .to in there when it's just as easy to remove it and not have to worry about what info is or is not available to the .to site owner?  It's easier and simpler to remove it and not take the chance.  I'm not just saying that for his benefit - because obviously if he's running Liberte, things are pretty secure, but I'm saying that because most people browsing with the .to in the url are NOT running Liberte or anything else for that matter -- most are simply browsing from the clearnet using the .to proxy to access onion sites.  And for THOSE people, yes, it is dangerous.

EDIT:

In fact, the .to proxy site itself warns users:

Quote
By using this service instead of connecting directly to the Tor network you are trading off security and anonymity for convenience. Know that we can identify the IP of visitors using this service (but chooses not to). We strongly recommended to access Tor Hidden Services directly using the Tor Browser Bundle to increase your security and anonymity.

Title: Re: under attack again
Post by: The ILF on April 28, 2013, 11:47 pm
onion.to is a web site that allows people to access hidden tor services *without* using tor.  It does this by passing them through a proxy that connects to the tor network.

If you access whateversite.onion.to without a tored connection, whoever it is that runs onion.to (apparently someone named XXor) can see your ip.

In addition, as far as we understand, going through onion.to allows the people running onion.to to see whatever data (i.e. everything on the page, including usernames, passwords, etc.) is being passed through, regardless of whether your initial connection to them is tored.  Think about it this way: if you access facebook over tor, obviously facebook still knows what credentials you've logged in with -- they just don't know your ip.

Besides onion.to, there is also tor2web.org and maybe some other sites that do the same thing.  Our way of thinking is that these sites are meant for people to be able to casually browse hidden services that contain static data (like leaked documents or something).  They protect the web publisher, but not the web browser.  And so they are definitely *not* meant for doing things like conducting business on SR.

And as for the government taking Sunday off, we weren't aware that we get a reprieve from police arrests or military bombings on the weekend.

tl;dr: Scout is 100% right.

P.S. DPR, keep on keeping on!

Title: Re: under attack again
Post by: SelfSovereignty on April 29, 2013, 07:17 am
Quote from: QualityMeds on April 29, 2013, 04:09 am
I still fail to see how a Ddos attack on a specific .onion site is even possible without knowing the specific server's location. Does this mean that someone has figured out where SR's servers are located? Bandwidth is limited for the Tor server volunteers, correct? Wouldn't an overload of data just make you lose connectivity with the Tor servers you are connected to? Am I wrong? If I'm right, what other possible method could someone have to slow down SR's servers to a crawl? Wow a lot of questions there, hope someone can answer some or all of them...

So as I often point out as a disclaimer before I go shooting my mouth off about this, I don't do cracking.  All this hacking and DoS rubbish just isn't my thing, but it's kind of related and kind of interesting, so I know a little bit about it.  Still: take my words with a grain of salt.  I'm no expert in this.

There are a ton of ways to perform a denial of service attack.  Some cripple a machine by hitting it with too many requests at once that the actual operating system isn't able to handle, some don't try to paralyze the operating system at all but instead try to overload the web server software so that *it* gets crippled, some try to exploit specific vulnerabilities in a database connection so that even if the server software is functioning properly the site is still crippled because the database storing all the information is crippled...  It goes on and on.  Lots of ways nobody even knows yet, I'm sure.  All of these systems are all interacting with each other using dozens of different standards and protocols.  It's almost a miracle it works as well as it does to begin with.

There are two basic network connection protocols, TCP and UDP.  TCP is what you usually think of an internet connection (like to a web page), and it's the connection type that Tor supports.  UDP is often used for denial of service attacks, but Tor doesn't even support that protocol.  You can't send information using UDP over Tor.  Well... I hate to speak in absolutes, but basically it's just not possible.

So that's why everyone goes around saying you can't do distributed denial of service attacks via Tor.  Because classically speaking, you can't.  But a denial of service denies access to a given service.  I don't know about you guys, but I'm sure as Hell being denied access to SR's forums.  It also doesn't seem to have anything at all to do with the Tor network.  The servers themselves are being (almost) crippled by a means other than what people usually are talking about when they say DDoS.

If you're really curious what may be going on, you can check out http://mixedbit.org/blog/2013/04/11/dos_attack_on_cdn_users.html -- I don't know that it has anything to do with anything here, but it may give you a better idea how a DoS can be done even with Tor.  Or it may just confuse you more, I dunno... either way, there ya go.

By the way, I've been on the main Silk Road sight all night.  Frankly I don't know what you guys are talking about, SR has been working just fine for me.  The forums on the other hand......

Title: Re: under attack again
Post by: Jediknight on April 29, 2013, 02:54 pm
There has to be a solution for this, otherwise TOR bundle is pure garbage.  . . someone should let the TOR people know that there is a flaw in their software and its volnerable to attacks.  They should've accounted for this type of attack (or maybe they did). . . 

This makes TOR useless it was designed to provide people with a means to speak out without being forced to be quiet.   Now, we see that freedom of speech can be controlled by others.  Any government can use the same attack to shut people up using TOR.

Its a dark day for mankind and liberal freedoms.
This jeopardizes the entire TOR concept.   Whats the purpose of onion sites then, if they can be censored so easily?

Any chance that the government or anyone has asked the TOR developers to write in a way to stop a rouge site or person- and now they are using it to stop this site?  Rollback the TOR software version to a previous version to see if a recent update has made an attack possible, or maybe it was possible all along and nobody exploited it yet?   

 I think TOR is behind this in some way.

My guess is:

-  the US military is testing out their new toys on us.  We are a testing website now for attack tools.   A fun challenge for others to attack.  They got the go ahead to cripple the site, or use it as a training tool.

- Internet warfare using brute force on enemy targets on the internet.  SR is a threat to American economy and conservative social views.  Its a fairly legit reason to attack us using military grade networking gear designed to cripple enemy networks. 

- People at TOR were asked to provide a means of stopping rouge websites on TOR in the name of national security.  They had a method all along, or just created one.

Libertarian views are taking a hit.

Post by: itsthecops on April 29, 2013, 07:28 pm
I'm an idiot, but . .
 I can't help but wonder why this whole ship is at dock?  It can still sail around the harbour quite safely for the time being.

Multiple URLS and switch between them would certainly work  its a reasonable idea.

Simple manual switching as a silly but functional idea:
 It must be a bit of work to reprogram the botnet's target address each time it changes.   At some point it will become tedious and they won't want to play anymore.   Post the latest URL in the forum, or some clearnet forum that can't be DDOSed as easily.  Users will keep up to the latest URL, don't worry they want their drugs.  they'll figure it out. .    It would only be temporary then switch back to normal when they stop.   At least the site would be accessible to a few people in the know.. .the rest can learn to keep up or just wait until the war is over. 

Either way, there is no reason the site can't continue to work on another unknown URL for the time being. .. until a solution can come.
Unless that is the tactic here. .  to get SIlk Road to come out from the woodwork.?

Unpublished alternate address:
I'm sure they got it worked out, but a backup site wouldn't hurt for days like this.  It can be a simple contact /order page /forwarder that works for any vendor.  This way buyers can at least order and check up on orders.  Vendors can use Access, or Excel or organize their offline orders.

Offline downloaded site:
An offline, downloadable version of the site can be done.   Browse the products at top speed all you want off your hard drive.   Orders can be sent to an intermediary at SR, who then forwards the order to the right vendor or something like that.  Its just temporary and would keep business flowing for the meantime.

Vendors pitch in for a site receptionist for when the site goes down:
I think vendors would gladly pitch in to pay for a staff person to handle orders manually as a backup solution when the site is down.  There are all sorts of options really.  I'm sure there are brilliant people with even better ideas to share.

Its time to start exploring arrangements rather than the ' all or nothing' approach.

Title: Re: under attack again
Post by: moopsr on April 29, 2013, 10:50 pm
Quote from: ProudCannabian on April 29, 2013, 09:33 pm
One thing we can look at is the IPs of exit nodes.
We can probably guess that IF this is Government sponsored they are running their own high-speed exit nodes to help facilitate the attack.
As a brief experiment we could DDoS only those nodes that appear like they might be part of the attack.

Like These servers:
conformal00 to conformal21(most suspicious to me because there are so many high speed nodes in sequence in the US)

chaoscomputerclub (german exit nodes, also numbered in sequence and high speed)

You get the idea.  Likely high-speed nodes in sequence, because they'd want to be able to identify and document their operation.
Don't do that, it won't solve anything.
Chaos computer club is a well-know hackers club in Germany, you should watch "23 - Nichts ist so wie es scheint", it's a movie about a true story of German hacker who belonged to the CCC, hacked several USA nuclear plants and sold it to the soviets, if I recall the story correctly.
It's an ooold club with tradition and enough power to have high capacity lines, they're probably not doing anything in behalf of any government.

Mind that: Clients who connect to the Silkroad are as untraceable as the Silkroad server is. The most probable thing is that nobody here will ever find out who is attacking the Silkroad so leave it be, forget about revenge, it brings nothing good to our image and will do more harm than good and will serve as an excuse for future attacks, which will take the site down for even more time.

We should focus on defense rather than an unfruitful knee-jerk reaction. I don't really know how DPR set up his servers but if I were to DoS/DDoS attack the Silkroad, I'd focus on successive HTTP GET/POST requests to the Silkroad server.
Contrary to what many people stated, servers behind tor are susceptible to these attacks and it's something very easy to perform. For example, if you download the same file over and over from Silkroad, you will hog the server's bandwidth the same way you could do it any other site on the internet.
And there's another problem for Silkroad being behind Tor: It cannot ban the flooders by IP address, since there are no IP address identifying anyone here; so Silkroad servers sits there helplessly waiting for the flood to stop.

A DDoS can not only work by hogging the server's bandwidth but it can also hog the Servers' RAM or CPU by forcing it to perform heavy operations. It could be by calling some PHP script on the road that perform some long operation on the database; while a normal user wouldn't be able to notice which operations take more or less time, a determined attacker could guess by statistical analysis how many time does it take to execute each operation and exploit it in order to put the CPUs or RAM under heavy load. If successful, the attacker

Of course most of these intensive scripts can only be ran after logging in, and you need to solve a captcha to login in but I can assure you that I would be able to make a program that breaks it very easily and I ain't no expert in solving captchas or anything like that. I'd advise you to change it as soon as you can.

This doesn't mean that the Silkroad was broken, at all. I'd be pretty confident that DPR did a good job regarding the users confidentiality. Don't worry because DDoS are the lowest of the lowest kind of "hacker" attacks. It's the desperate cry of someone who could do nothing better to break a system, like the cry of a baby who was denied some candy. Every system is susceptible to DDoS attacks!

Another idea that I'd like to leave, and that I'm assuming you have physical access to the SR servers, is that if you don't have logs of your system, you could build a one-way ethernet cable from the SR server to a Log server that would only allow you to write to the Log server, and never read. That would make impossible even for the leetest hacker in the world to read the logs from a remote source.
This way you would be able to inspect the nature of future attacks and don't open any hole in your system.
You could add an extra layer of security by encrypting the logs in the Log server.

Have fun!

I feel 95% safe due to I see that service like this has never been intercepted by Law Enforcement in hacking way. Farmers Market has been shut down because guys offered too many ways of payment like Western Union, Paypal etc. + communication has been supported by Hushmail which is not totally anonymous so they caught them in classic methods of interception like tracing payments or reading their letters.
I hope that everything will be fixed soon and few words to people are talking about proxy websites like onion.to and they say it's risky. It's risky only from this side that your ISP will see what adress you enter but all communication from entrance node through relay nodes to exit nodes and then to server is encrypted so it's 100% safe. You don't have to even worry if LE close website due to they will only receive encrypted packages of data which has to be cracked to see what does it contain and TOR nodes don't remember what they received and what they sent so it's really safe system. Weakness part of TOR is logg in to clearnet websites because exit node can be listened and they can intercept packages from exit nodes and decrypt it but only if connection is not encrypted.

Quote from: Dread Pirate Roberts on April 28, 2013, 09:57 am
UPDATE (04/30/2013 0035 UTC): We have come a long way in the battle, but still do not have the upper hand.  It's looking more and more like a restructuring of the tor software or even the tor network will be required to mitigate the kind of attack we are under.  If this can be solved by modifying the tor client software running the silk road .onion, then it will be a matter of patching and redeploying the hidden service.  If it is a network issue, it will require the cooperation of the Tor developers, or running a new network of nodes.  I haven't given up hope for a faster solution, but if one can not be found, then we will move to a semi private scheme where users will be given access through many private URLs.  I'll keep everyone updated on how we will move forward, but please be prepared for a few more days at the least of no access.

UPDATE (04/29/2013 0715 UTC): Just want to let you all know I'm still here and we're still doing battle behind the scenes to get the forums and main site running again.  It is incredibly discouraging to have everything we've worked so hard for taken down by some anonymous and malevolent person, but your kind words of encouragement do wonders for our moral.  We are on the cutting edge of anonymity technology here.  The attacks being used against us MUST be overcome if Silk Road and any anonymous public sites are to have a future.  Thank you again for your patience with all of this, and pray that we make it through stronger than we started.

We are being attacked once more.  This time the forums are under attack as well.  Access is intermittent, so hopefully some of you can read this.  We are doing everything possible to overcome this latest attack.  Please be patient while we find a solution.

Title: Re: under attack again
Post by: PuretyAboveAll on April 30, 2013, 02:07 am
Quote from: TwoHat on April 30, 2013, 01:39 am
Quote from: PuretyAboveAll on April 30, 2013, 01:14 am
Who benefits from these attacks on SR? If any at all...

I can't help but notice, that every time SK is attacked the price on BC goes up. Coincidence?

The "who benefits from these attacks" in this case is like your typical "follow the money". There's only 3 potential beneficial situations and beneficiaries.

1) If it's a competing market, the motive is to gain new users defunct from SR, particularly vendors.
2) If it's people who hold a large sum of bitcoin, the motive is to drive the price up and sell.
3) If it's people who want to buy a large sum of bitcoin, the motive is to drive the price down and buy.

My money, so to speak. Is on no.2: Someone with a vast quantity of BC' s that they are trying to sell at the highest rate possible. Maybe it is Max Keiser  ;D

For the other techies in here that want to learn more about possible attacks on the tor network, scroll to chapter 7:
Warning Clearnet Link!: https://svn.torproject.org/svn/tor/trunk/doc/design-paper/tor-design.html

Thinking about clearnet links, i hope you have a very very secure hoster that protects your personal information. Something like cyberbunker.

Its difficult tough to give advice as DPR doesnt really sayed much about the actual type of attack, but i would guess they are attackin rendezvous/introduction points.

Title: Re: under attack again
Post by: Mcrad on April 30, 2013, 04:52 am
Quote from: Dread Pirate Roberts on April 28, 2013, 09:57 am
UPDATE (04/30/2013 0035 UTC): We have come a long way in the battle, but still do not have the upper hand.  It's looking more and more like a restructuring of the tor software or even the tor network will be required to mitigate the kind of attack we are under.  If this can be solved by modifying the tor client software running the silk road .onion, then it will be a matter of patching and redeploying the hidden service.  If it is a network issue, it will require the cooperation of the Tor developers, or running a new network of nodes.  I haven't given up hope for a faster solution, but if one can not be found, then we will move to a semi private scheme where users will be given access through many private URLs.  I'll keep everyone updated on how we will move forward, but please be prepared for a few more days at the least of no access.

UPDATE (04/29/2013 0715 UTC): Just want to let you all know I'm still here and we're still doing battle behind the scenes to get the forums and main site running again.  It is incredibly discouraging to have everything we've worked so hard for taken down by some anonymous and malevolent person, but your kind words of encouragement do wonders for our moral.  We are on the cutting edge of anonymity technology here.  The attacks being used against us MUST be overcome if Silk Road and any anonymous public sites are to have a future.  Thank you again for your patience with all of this, and pray that we make it through stronger than we started.

We are being attacked once more.  This time the forums are under attack as well.  Access is intermittent, so hopefully some of you can read this.  We are doing everything possible to overcome this latest attack.  Please be patient while we find a solution.

Title: Re: under attack again
Post by: Sc0t1and_Y4rdi3 on April 30, 2013, 10:34 am
Quote from: TwoHat on April 30, 2013, 04:31 am
I found a few articles on clearnet that are related to preventing selective DOS of a TOR service. The last article contains a post by the author of pyLoris that describes his recommendations for mitigating DOS from pyLoris and Tor in general. I hope one of these helps. I will be doing as much research as I can to help find a solution.

hxxp://arxiv.org/pdf/1107.3863.pdf

"Anonymous communication systems are subject to selective denial-of-service (DoS) attacks. Selective DoS attacks lower anonymity as they force paths to be rebuilt multiple times to ensure delivery which increases the opportunity for more attack. In this paper we present a detection algorithm that filters out compromised communication channels for one of the anonymity networks, Tor. Our detection algorithm uses two levels of probing to filter out potentially com-promised tunnels. We perform probabilistic analysis and extensive simulation to
show the robustness of our detection algorithm. We also analyze the overhead of our detection algorithm and show that we can achieve satisfactory security guar-antee for reasonable communication overhead (~5% of the total available Tor bandwidth). Real world experiments reveal that our detection algorithm provides good defense against selective DoS attack."

hxxp://fc09.ifca.ai/papers/43_Detecting_dos_in_tor.pdf

"More recently, Borisov et al. [3] showed that an adversary willing to engage in denial of service (DoS) could increase their probability of compromising anonymity. When a path is
reconstructed after a denial of service, new proxies are chosen, and thus the adversary has another chance to be on the endpoints of the path. Our contributions are as follows. We prove that an adversary engaging in the DoS attack in an idealized Tor-like system can be detected by probing at most 3n paths in the system, where n is the number of proxies in the system. Through simulation, we show that an adversary attempting to avoid detection by engaging in DoS probabilistically can still be detected, and that the attempt to avoid detection radically degrades the effectiveness of the attack. Finally, using measurements of connection drop rates across Tor nodes, we implement a version of the detection algorithm and conclude it is unlikely that such an attack was in progress during the time period the network was observed."

hxxp://security.stackexchange.com/questions/19698/mitigating-anonymous-dos-tor-combined-with-pyloris

"sarepta: To start off, I am the author of PyLoris, so I have done a good amount of research into this. In fact, the attack you have envisioned is one that I specifically coded to when developing PyLoris--the current version even comes bundled with an helper app tor_switcher.py which routes the attack through multiple Tor exit nodes.

The only good way of detecting a Tor-based flood is by checking source IP addresses against known Tor exit nodes. This is trivial with blacklisting or plugins like mod_security. In my research, mod_antilors does not prevent the PyLoris+Tor vector as it is IP address based. My personal choice for preventing this attack is to use any server other than Apache to handle direct connections from the internet. This could mean using a reverse proxy like Varnish to marshal requests or switching to something like nginx for your web server.

Aside from rethinking your infrastructure, I do feel that a combination of low timeouts, IP connection limits, minimum data transfer rates, maximum connection time limits, and maximum request sizes can provide adequate protection from this form of attack. I say this all with the disclaimer that there is no way to prevent this form of attack, and that these configurations should be thought through thoroughly to gauge their impact on a per-server basis."

please shut up

It's interesting to look at Atlas - some of the highest bandwidth TOR nodes online right now all show a burst in traffic starting just about when the most recent DOS started.

These nodes in particular:
https://atlas.torproject.org/#details/80F870DD215A0C56005266A71C46F92F39F1973B
https://atlas.torproject.org/#details/0ECBAB33DD27A6DA5C1141B39F839F931F92334C
https://atlas.torproject.org/#details/D0236B1908B3CC686DB0A361F4931073A25793F1
https://atlas.torproject.org/#details/43691853EA556C21A77E006886A5DC579855F527

It could be that these in particular are listed among the highest bandwidth nodes currently simply because they're being used to pass on DOS traffic to SR, but they certainly show a traffic pattern not visible on the other high bandwidth nodes, and between them they're topping a gigabit in traffic...

Title: Re: under attack again
Post by: users_dont_lose_drugs on April 30, 2013, 03:03 pm
Well, Ive hit Jr Forum member status, so I thought I would celebrate with a big fuck off TLDR stating some of my thoughts about my life and the road. Some of you might find it interesting, Im basically bored at work so I thought it would be worth sharing with you lot (who are all awesome by the way).
The road has presented some interesting times in my life over the last 7 months or so. I started out buying standard recreational weekend drugs that I had difficulty getting hold of IRL. Then after a few transactions that went extremely well, started also using it exclusively for all my drugs such as cannabis and vals to aid me after my Friday night binge.
I am strictly a weekend warrior when it comes to drugs, so I feel for those of you who have deeper dependency than myself (and am not really qualified to present any feedback or strategies for dependence management). But I wanted to share my habits with you all. I believe that the reason I came to the road was because I was always forward thinking with my drug buying. I hated the people who were so short sighted with buying drugs, when I asked a group of friends if they wanted in theyd be like well, its 10:00AM on a Tuesday, and I cant imagine what I will feel like at 10:30 PM on Friday after 5 beers  I dont fancy any now so, no Ill be fine. Then sure enough Friday rolls round and drinks after work everyone is like can we go 2s on that bag you got?
So I think theres an element of that when SR goes down, it fucks with our planning; DPR has created a platform that beats buying contraband IRL. SR has been such a pleasure to use, I have done Xx + transactions and all have been flawless.
We know its going to be good quality, and are protected by Escrow.
I was here last Nov when it all went tits up and people claimed DPR ran off with all the coins. Its true since then hes bounced back after every setback that followed Nov.  But it seems this is his most challenging problem to date, based on his last update.  I have no reason to doubt DPR based on his track record in recent months, but all theories aside this might simply be out of his hands. I wish him and his team all the best.
Anyways, just my experiences on here, pointless blather really, but thought worth sharing.
Wish we lived in a more free world.

Title: Re: under attack again
Post by: RootZero on April 30, 2013, 06:04 pm
From my understanding Tor has always been at risk of DoS'ing of hidden services as its impossible to determine legitimate traffic from from malicious due to the anonymous nature of Tor.

The ultimate solution would be to install more hardware and entry points to meet the increased demand for bandwidth and server power, however if it's a DDoS attack from a botnet, its unlikely that would help as no amount of bandwidth will cut it.

If it is a DDoS, which seems the most likely, the perpetrators won't be able to keep it up forever. Paying for use of a botnet isn't exactly cheap.

Another solution, which DPR mentioned is using multiple urls, this seems like the best option to me. Rotate new urls repeatedly and the botnet won't keep up. The difficulty is issuing those urls to users, I'm sure there's a solution there somewhere but it needs some thinking outside the box.

Title: Re: under attack again
Post by: cyanspore on April 30, 2013, 09:55 pm
BMR has a certification process to verify if the same username vendor is the same on BMR and SR by sending a PM via BMR, they then send another PM with code via SR and you get certified on BMR with a mark on your user name in your profile at BMR.

This of course, means that BMR has been working in concert with Silk Road to verify that vendors who say they are the same, actually are the same. I did this, and you can see my verification icon at BMR, link in sig

They are doing this now because many vendors who got banned became a vendor under another name of a vendor who was still legit here. So basically both BMR and SR teamed up to help cut down on fraud

I started out at BMR because I could not afford to become a vendor here until another vendor lent me 5BTC so I could come here. I paid him back in 10 days flat after coming here. There maybe have been and maybe still are scammers at BMR, but they have been banning vendors over there, but it's also a very tiny traffic site compared with SR

But there are some who are on both site and have been verified using a special SR account set up for this. It also means it's highly unlikely the attacks are coming from people at BMR since they have already been working together in at least this small way

Apparently this is not widely known, although there are threads at BMR about it. You can see the little green camel underneath my  profile icon at BMR here

http://5onwnspjvuk7cwvk.onion/index.php?p=viewUser&id=166446

Here is the announcement of this feature on BMR forums

http://fec33nz6mhzd54zj.onion/viewtopic.php?id=2785

Have you considered that this attack isn't just against Silk Road but against the very nature of TOR Hidden Services?  Changes to the TOR code are probably required in order to defeat this attack.  Keep in mind changing the code could have security implications for Silk Road and DPR.

Why hasn't this attack been utilized in the past by an attacker?  Maybe The TOR Project made a mistake by publicly describing some of the faults with Hidden Services last week in their blog.  Perhaps the attacker only learned of these vulnerabilities recently.

From the blog
Quote
One of the main problems with a busy Hidden Service is that its Introduction Points will get hammered by clients. Since Introduction Points are regular Tor relays, they are not intended to handle such load.

The adversarial version of the previous section involves attackers intentionally hammering the Introduction Points of a Hidden Service to make it unreachable by honest clients. This means that an attacker can temporarily bring down a Hidden Service by DoSing a small number of Tor relays
So is Silk Road technically under attack or is the TOR network actually under attack?

And I think the worst case scenario has been expressed already by DPR:
Quote
we will move to a semi private scheme where users will be given access through many private URLs

Title: Re: under attack again
Post by: Intraday Cosmonaut on May 01, 2013, 05:33 am
Quote from: Dread Pirate Roberts on April 28, 2013, 09:57 am
UPDATE (05/01/2013 0238 UTC): Silk Road is open and accessible.  As soon as the attacker finds out, he will likely change his tactics and try to take the site down again.  Hopefully he won't be able to, but time will tell.

UPDATE (04/30/2013 2022 UTC): Still working on a solution.  I haven't given up hope that we will be able to go forward as a public market without limiting access.  We are putting all of our efforts into making that a reality.  If that changes, I will let you know here.

UPDATE (04/30/2013 0035 UTC): We have come a long way in the battle, but still do not have the upper hand.  It's looking more and more like a restructuring of the tor software or even the tor network will be required to mitigate the kind of attack we are under.  If this can be solved by modifying the tor client software running the silk road .onion, then it will be a matter of patching and redeploying the hidden service.  If it is a network issue, it will require the cooperation of the Tor developers, or running a new network of nodes.  I haven't given up hope for a faster solution, but if one can not be found, then we will move to a semi private scheme where users will be given access through many private URLs.  I'll keep everyone updated on how we will move forward, but please be prepared for a few more days at the least of no access.

UPDATE (04/29/2013 0715 UTC): Just want to let you all know I'm still here and we're still doing battle behind the scenes to get the forums and main site running again.  It is incredibly discouraging to have everything we've worked so hard for taken down by some anonymous and malevolent person, but your kind words of encouragement do wonders for our moral.  We are on the cutting edge of anonymity technology here.  The attacks being used against us MUST be overcome if Silk Road and any anonymous public sites are to have a future.  Thank you again for your patience with all of this, and pray that we make it through stronger than we started.

We are being attacked once more.  This time the forums are under attack as well.  Access is intermittent, so hopefully some of you can read this.  We are doing everything possible to overcome this latest attack.  Please be patient while we find a solution.

/bows humbly

excellent work dpr. thankyou.

Title: Re: under attack again
Post by: fitness_n_herb on May 02, 2013, 01:33 pm
Calm heads prevail.

When you select the button on Tor "New Identity" that changes your location, thus a new chance of getting on.

If you have tried a few new identities and still no go, (1) Restart Tor, completely stop the service, then restart it.
(2) Smoke a bowl, watch a show, give it 1hr or so, and return ON a new identity.

Basic troubleshooting folks!
:)

-F&H

I think the error is a good sign, actually. An error page instead of just a connection timeout means that the server is failing gracefully. It's a visible sign of the progress that DPR and crew are making behind the scenes to withstand and/or recover from this attack.

An analogy: You haven't seen your friend in a long time, and you're getting worried. You go to his place and knock on the door. Consider the two following results:

1. Your friend talks through the door and tells you that he's super-sick right now and he doesn't want to open the door and breathe his horrible germs on you.

2. There is no response.

Which would you prefer?

Title: Re: under attack again
Post by: vektor the pirate on May 03, 2013, 11:13 pm
I as well saw the page with the HTTP HOST information.  It basically had my TOR IP, and then the IP of the HTTP host.  I actually took that IP, ran a port scan on it and found that port 22 (SSH) and port 443 (HTTPS) were open.  I went ahead dropped the IP in a regular browser, put https:// before it and then that 403 Forbidden (nginx) message appeared.  The information also showed the internal folder structure of the website for example (var\www\****\*****)  It was deeply concerning at first but honestly I think the IP address of one of the many reverse proxies were revealed.  I researched what nginx is and found the following :

"nginx (pronounced "engine x") is an open source web server and a reverse proxy server for HTTP, SMTP, POP3, and IMAP protocols, with a strong focus on high concurrency, performance and low memory usage. It is licensed under a BSD-like license and it runs on Unix, Linux, BSD variants, Mac OS X, Solaris, AIX, HP-UX, and Microsoft Windows."


So it is possible that all that was leaked was one of the many reverse proxy servers that are used through tor to get to the eventual final destination.  I really do hope that was what it was.  I was literally getting the same 403 forbidden message that I get sometimes through tor when having issues accessing the road, except this was through internet explorer and hitting the revealead web ip.

I really hope this isn't a government attack that is trying to extract server info/ip through and advanced hacking method.  It is probably possible.

Post by: scout on May 06, 2013, 10:33 pm
Quote from: TurpenT on May 06, 2013, 06:44 pm
The site seems to have more bugs than ever before, BUT IT'S FUNCTIONAL! So who's complaining?

But really, does anyone know why the site has been buggy? I mean I've never been logged out so many times. On top of that the captcha is merely 3 numbers, instead of the 4 letter 2-3 number captcha we're used to. Am I just being paranoid, or is that weird?


For those who have been here for several months, that 3-character captcha is not as worrying because we've seen it happen before without consequence.  It's just a weird little glitch, but it's not dangerous.  If you refresh the login page, you'll get a captcha of normal length.  As long as the url is correct (silkroadvb5piz3r.onion) and you are not being asked for your PIN, then you're fine.

Also - before anyone brings it up here (as it's already all over the forums) - YES, there are delays in bitcoin deposits! 

DPR is aware of these issues.
